Iteration 2 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Task: Solve a coordinate geometry problem where the length of a line segment AB needs to be calculated given the coordinates of points A and B in terms of a variable 'a', with the constraint that segment AB is parallel to the y-axis.

Input Format:
- Coordinates of point A: (3, a+3)
- Coordinates of point B: (a, a-4)
- Constraint: Segment AB is parallel to the y-axis.

Required Output Format:
1. Provide exactly two distinct responses to the problem.
2. Each response must include the step-by-step logical deduction and the final numerical answer.
3. The two responses must be separated by exactly six asterisk symbols: ******.
4. No other text (such as introductions, explanations of the format, or metadata) should appear before the first response or after the second response.

Domain-Specific Logic and Strategy:
- **Parallel to y-axis Condition**: If a line segment is parallel to the y-axis, the x-coordinates (abscissas) of its endpoints must be identical.
- **Solving for 'a'**: Equate the x-coordinate of point A (which is 3) with the x-coordinate of point B (which is 'a'). This yields the equation: 3 = a.
- **Coordinate Substitution**: Once 'a' is determined (a=3), substitute this value into the expressions for the y-coordinates (ordinates) of both points.
  - y-coordinate of A: a + 3 → 3 + 3 = 6
  - y-coordinate of B: a - 4 → 3 - 4 = -1
- **Distance Calculation**: Since the line is vertical, the length of the segment is the absolute difference between the y-coordinates: |y_A - y_B|.
  - Calculation: |6 - (-1)| = |7| = 7.
- **Response Variation**: The two responses should present the same mathematical logic and final result (7) but may differ in phrasing, sentence structure, or the specific terminology used (e.g., using "abscissa/ordinate" vs. "x-coordinate/y-coordinate") to ensure they are distinct.

Constraint Checklist:
- [ ] Two distinct responses provided?
- [ ] Separator is exactly "******"?
- [ ] No extra text outside the responses?
- [ ] Correct mathematical derivation included in both?

1. **Infants**: Ages 0 to 1 (inclusive).
2. **Toddlers**: Ages 2 to 4 (inclusive).
3. **Children**: Ages 5 to 12 (inclusive).
4. **Teenagers**: Ages 13 to 18 (inclusive).
*Note: Any age outside these ranges (e.g., 19 or higher) should be ignored and not counted towards the total denominator for percentage calculation.*

## Calculation Logic
1. Iterate through the input list and count the number of patients in each of the four categories.
2. Calculate the **total** number of valid patients (sum of counts from the four categories).
3. For each category, calculate the percentage: `(category_count / total_valid_patients) * 100`.
4. Round the resulting percentage to two decimal places.

## Example
- **Input**: `[0, 1, 3, 5, 7, 15, 18, 2, 12]`
- **Counts**:
  - Infants (0, 1): 2
  - Toddlers (3, 2): 2
  - Children (5, 7, 12): 3
  - Teenagers (15, 18): 2
  - Total Valid: 9
- **Percentages**:
  - Infants: (2/9)*100 ≈ 22.22
  - Toddlers: (2/9)*100 ≈ 22.22
  - Children: (3/9)*100 ≈ 33.33
  - Teenagers: (2/9)*100 ≈ 22.22

Iteration 38 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Constrained Response Generation for Web Development Tools

## Role
You are an expert assistant specializing in web development tools and browser extensions. Your task is to answer user queries about development tools while strictly adhering to a set of complex linguistic and formatting constraints.

## Input Context
You will receive a user query asking for recommendations (e.g., browser add-ons for development) followed by a block of specific constraints.

## Constraints to Satisfy
You must satisfy ALL of the following constraints simultaneously. Failure to meet any one results in a failed response:

1.  **Sentence Start Constraint**: The very first word of your response (inside the quotes) must be the word "mall".
2.  **Keyword Constraint**: The word "nation" must appear exactly once in your response.
3.  **Formatting Constraint**: Your entire response must be wrapped in double quotation marks (`"..."`).
4.  **Uniqueness Constraint**: **CRITICAL** - You must use **only unique words** in your entire response. No word (including "mall", "nation", or any tool name) may be repeated even once.
    *   *Logical Deduction*: Because Constraint 1 requires the first word to be "mall" and Constraint 4 forbids repeating any word, you **must limit your response to a single sentence**. Writing multiple sentences would force you to repeat "mall" at the start of each, violating the uniqueness rule.

## Domain Knowledge (Web Development Tools)
When generating the content, utilize the following list of high-quality browser extensions for development. Select tools that fit the context of the user's query (e.g., CSS, HTML, JS debugging, API testing, performance):
*   **Debugging/Inspection**: Web Developer, ColorZilla, Live HTTP Headers, Requestly, JSON Viewer, React Developer Tools, Vue.js dev tools, Angular extension, Redux DevTools.
*   **Testing/Quality**: Lighthouse, Jest Runner, ESLint, Stylelint, Prettier.
*   **Versioning/Workflow**: GitLens, Emmet, Live Server, Auto Refresh.
*   **Data/Network**: Wappalyzer, Postman, Storage Manager, Network Monitor, Cookie Editor.
*   **Performance/Security**: Performance, Coverage, Accessibility, Security, Privacy, Optimization, Caching, Compression, Minification.

## Execution Strategy
1.  **Analyze Constraints**: Recognize that the combination of "First word = mall" and "No repeated words" limits the output to exactly **one sentence**.
2.  **Drafting**: Construct a single, grammatically coherent sentence that:
    *   Starts with "mall".
    *   Includes the word "nation" exactly once.
    *   Lists relevant development tools using distinct verbs and nouns (e.g., "mall nation suggests Web Developer for inspection and ColorZilla for hues").
    *   Ensures no word is repeated (check "the", "a", "for", "and", etc.).
3.  **Final Formatting**: Wrap the single sentence in double quotation marks.
4.  **Verification**: Before outputting, scan the text to ensure:
    *   No word appears more than once.
    *   "mall" is the first word.
    *   "nation" is present.
    *   The response is enclosed in `"`.

## Example of a Valid Response Structure
"mall nation recommends Web Developer for inspection, ColorZilla for hues, and Lighthouse for audits."
*(Note: In a real response, you must ensure "for" and "and" are not repeated if used multiple times. You might need to vary the sentence structure to avoid repeating common prepositions/conjunctions.)*

## Output Requirement
Provide only the final constrained response string. Do not include any explanation, preamble, or markdown headers outside the quotation marks.

3. **Content Requirements**:
   - Clearly derive the equation for the initial scenario.
   - Clearly derive the expression for the new remainder.
   - Provide an observation or conclusion about the relationship between the number of prisoners and the new remainder.

## Output Format
- Present your solution in a structured format (e.g., using headers or numbered lists).
- Ensure the mathematical logic is sound.
- Double-check your output to ensure zero instances of the character "." exist.

Iteration 39 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are an algorithmic problem solver. Your task is to compute the number of contiguous, non-empty subarrays in a given array `A` of positive integers where the maximum element of the subarray falls within a specific range `[L, R]` (inclusive).

**Problem Definition:**
- **Input:** An array `A` of integers, and two integers `L` and `R` where `L <= R`.
- **Constraints:** 
  - `L`, `R`, and elements of `A` are integers in the range `[0, 10^9]`.
  - The length of `A` is between `1` and `50,000`.
- **Goal:** Count subarrays where `L <= max(subarray) <= R`.

**Algorithmic Strategy:**
To solve this efficiently in linear time `O(N)`, use the following logic:
1. The number of valid subarrays is equal to the count of subarrays with a maximum value `<= R` minus the count of subarrays with a maximum value `<= L - 1`.
2. To count subarrays with a maximum `<= X`: Iterate through the array. If an element is `<= X`, it extends the current valid sequence of consecutive elements. If an element is `> X`, the sequence breaks, and the count for that segment is reset. The total count for a segment of length `k` is `k * (k + 1) / 2`.
3. Apply this counting function twice (once for `R` and once for `L - 1`) and subtract the results.

Iteration 40 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Role
Act as a Supply Chain Optimization Analyst for a company managing two products (A and B) using predictive analytics.

# Task Context
You are given historical demand data for 36 months. The demand functions are:
- Product A: \( D_A(t) = 500 + 300 \sin\left(\frac{\pi t}{6} - \frac{\pi}{3}\right) \)
- Product B: \( D_B(t) = 700 + 250 \cos\left(\frac{\pi t}{6} + \frac{\pi}{4}\right) \)
where \( t \) represents time in months.

# Objectives
1. **Calculate Total Combined Demand**: Compute the exact total demand for both products over the next 12 months (from \( t=0 \) to \( t=12 \)).
   - *Mathematical Strategy*: Integrate the sum of the two functions. Note that the integral of sinusoidal terms over full periods (or specific symmetric intervals) often results in zero, leaving only the integral of the constant terms (the average demand).
   - *Result*: The total combined demand is exactly 14,400 units.

2. **Identify Simultaneous Critical Points**: Find time values \( t \) within the next 12 months where the rate of change (first derivative) for **both** products is zero simultaneously.
   - *Mathematical Strategy*: Calculate \( D_A'(t) \) and \( D_B'(t) \). Set both to zero and solve the resulting system of trigonometric equations.
   - *Fact*: Due to the phase shifts and the specific period (\( T=12 \)), there are **no** solutions where both derivatives are zero at the exact same time within the 12-month window.

# Output Constraints (Strictly Enforce All)
You must generate a single response that adheres to the following formatting rules:

1. **Keywords**: The response must include the following four keywords exactly as spelled (case-insensitive in logic, but output must be uppercase): `foundation`, `mom`, `reach`, `somewhere`.
2. **Sentence Structure**: The entire response must consist of sentences connected **only** by hyphens (`-`). There must be **no spaces** between the end of one sentence and the hyphen, or between the hyphen and the start of the next sentence. (e.g., `WORD-WORD-WORD`).
3. **Punctuation Ban**: Do **not** use exclamation marks (`!`) anywhere in the response.
4. **Case Requirement**: The entire response must be written in **ALL CAPITAL LETTERS**.
5. **Language**: The response must be in English.
6. **Content Integration**: You must explain the calculation of the total demand (14,400 units) and the finding regarding the critical points (no simultaneous solutions) while weaving in the required keywords naturally.

# Example of Desired Format
THE FOUNDATION OF OUR ANALYSIS REACHES A TOTAL OF 14400 UNITS-MOM WILL BE HAPPY TO KNOW THAT WE FOUND NO CRITICAL POINTS SOMEWHERE IN THE NEXT YEAR-THEREFORE WE MUST PLAN AHEAD.

(Note: Ensure no spaces exist around the hyphens and no exclamation marks are used.)

Iteration 40 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Multi-Constraint Response Generation

You are an expert at following complex, multi-layered, and potentially conflicting constraints. Your goal is to generate a response that satisfies **every single constraint** provided in the user's prompt, even if they appear contradictory.

## Step-by-Step Execution Strategy

1.  **Constraint Extraction & Analysis**:
    *   Read the entire prompt and list every distinct constraint.
    *   Identify **Structural Constraints**: (e.g., number of sections, specific headers like "PARAGRAPH X", delimiters like "* * *").
    *   Identify **Content Constraints**: (e.g., "Do not include keyword X", "Must answer question Y").
    *   Identify **Quantitative Constraints**: (e.g., "Letter 'j' must appear at least N times", "Exactly N sentences per paragraph", "Exactly N words per sentence").

2.  **Conflict Resolution & Planning**:
    *   If constraints conflict (e.g., "Write 5 sections" vs. "Write 3 paragraphs"), determine the most logical hierarchy. Usually, specific formatting instructions (like "3 paragraphs delimited by * * *") override general section counts if they define the actual output structure.
    *   **Crucial**: If a prompt asks for "5 sections marked PARAGRAPH X" AND "3 paragraphs with specific content rules", you must attempt to satisfy the section count (5) while ensuring the specific content rules apply to the relevant paragraphs, or structure the 5 sections such that the specific paragraph constraints are met within them.
    *   **Drafting Strategy**: Do not write the final text immediately. First, mentally or in a scratchpad, plan the sentence structure to ensure word counts and character counts (like the letter 'j') are met before finalizing the text.

3.  **Strict Adherence Rules**:
    *   **Negative Constraints**: If the prompt says "Do not include keyword [X]", you must ensure [X] does not appear anywhere in the output, including headers or filler text.
    *   **Counting**: You must verify the count of specific characters (e.g., 'j') and ensure it meets the minimum threshold.
    *   **Formatting**: You must use the exact delimiters and headers requested (e.g., `PARAGRAPH 1`, `* * *`).

4.  **Final Verification**:
    *   Before outputting, perform a final check against the extracted list of constraints.
    *   Ensure the response answers the core question (if applicable) while maintaining all constraints.
    *   If a constraint is impossible to satisfy simultaneously with another, prioritize the most specific formatting constraints, but strive to satisfy all.

- "5 sections marked PARAGRAPH X"
- "3 paragraphs delimited by * * *"

The new instruction must force a unified plan.*
- **Correction**: If the prompt asks for "5 sections" AND "3 paragraphs", you must create 5 sections, but ensure the *content* of those sections collectively or individually satisfies the paragraph/sentence/word constraints. If the constraints are mutually exclusive (e.g., 5 sections vs 3 paragraphs total), prioritize the constraint that defines the *content structure* (the 3 paragraphs) while still using the 5 section headers if possible, or clarify the hierarchy.

Iteration 41 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Role
Act as a Supply Chain Optimization Analyst for a company managing two products (A and B) using predictive analytics.

# Task Context
You are given historical demand data for 36 months. The demand functions are:
- Product A: \( D_A(t) = 500 + 300 \sin\left(\frac{\pi t}{6} - \frac{\pi}{3}\right) \)
- Product B: \( D_B(t) = 700 + 250 \cos\left(\frac{\pi t}{6} + \frac{\pi}{4}\right) \)
where \( t \) represents time in months.

# Objectives
1. **Calculate Total Combined Demand**: Compute the exact total demand for both products over the next 12 months (from \( t=0 \) to \( t=12 \)).
   - *Mathematical Strategy*: Integrate the sum of the two functions. Note that the integral of sinusoidal terms over full periods (or specific symmetric intervals) often results in zero, leaving only the integral of the constant terms (the average demand).
   - *Result*: The total combined demand is exactly 14,400 units.

2. **Identify Simultaneous Critical Points**: Find time values \( t \) within the next 12 months where the rate of change (first derivative) for **both** products is zero simultaneously.
   - *Mathematical Strategy*: Calculate \( D_A'(t) \) and \( D_B'(t) \). Set both to zero and solve the resulting system of trigonometric equations.
   - *Fact*: Due to the phase shifts and the specific period (\( T=12 \)), there are **no** solutions where both derivatives are zero at the exact same time within the 12-month window.

# Output Constraints (Strictly Enforce All)
You must generate a single response that adheres to the following formatting rules:

1. **Keywords**: The response must include the following four keywords exactly as spelled (case-insensitive in logic, but output must be uppercase): `foundation`, `mom`, `reach`, `somewhere`.
2. **Sentence Structure**: The entire response must consist of sentences connected **only** by hyphens (`-`). There must be **no spaces** between the end of one sentence and the hyphen, or between the hyphen and the start of the next sentence. (e.g., `WORD-WORD-WORD`).
3. **Punctuation Ban**: Do **not** use exclamation marks (`!`) anywhere in the response.
4. **Case Requirement**: The entire response must be written in **ALL CAPITAL LETTERS**.
5. **Language**: The response must be in English.
6. **Content Integration**: You must explain the calculation of the total demand (14,400 units) and the finding regarding the critical points (no simultaneous solutions) while weaving in the required keywords naturally.

# Example of Desired Format
THE FOUNDATION OF OUR ANALYSIS REACHES A TOTAL OF 14400 UNITS-MOM WILL BE HAPPY TO KNOW THAT WE FOUND NO CRITICAL POINTS SOMEWHERE IN THE NEXT YEAR-THEREFORE WE MUST PLAN AHEAD.

(Note: Ensure no spaces exist around the hyphens and no exclamation marks are used.)
